        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus has come to our attention as the anode material for lithium-ion batteries with high theor. specific capacity of 2596 mAh g-1 due to its earth-abundant and low-cost.  However, it suffers from low electrocond. and large vol. expansion, resulting in serious capacity fading.  In this study, we confined red phosphorus nanoparticles into the hierarchical porous carbonaceous fibers to enhance its cycling stability.  Red phosphorus nanoparticles preferentially filled in the micropores and gradually extended to the larger pores.  The optimized electrochem. performance benefits from hierarchical pores filled with the appropriate content of red phosphorus, where the small micropores are used to confine the red phosphorus nanoparticles and the large mesopores are beneficial for the increased contact of electrolyte.  This can remit excessive vol. change and facilitate the contact area of electrolyte effectively.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchically porous carbon/red phosphorus composite for high-capacity sodium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Meng; Feng, Na; Liu, Mengmeng; Cong, Zifeng; Sun, Jiangman; Du, Chunhua; Liu, Quanbin; Pu, Xiong; Hu, Weiguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science Bulletin</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">63</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus has received remarkable attention as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) due to its high theor. capacity.  However, its practical application has been impeded by its intrinsic low electronic cond. and large vol. variations during sodiation/desodiation process.  Here, we design a composite to confine nanosized red phosphorus into the hierarchically porous carbon (HPC) walls by a vaporization-condensation strategy.  The mass loading of P in the HPC/P composite is optimized to deliver a reversible specific capacity of 2,202 mAh/gp based on the mass of red P (836 mAh/gcomposite based on the total composite mass), a high capacity retention over 77% after 100 cycles, and excellent rate performance of 929 mAh/gp at 2 C.  The hierarchical porous carbon serves as the conductive networks, downsize the red phosphorus to nanoscale, and provide free space to accommodate the large vol. expansions.  The suppressed mech. failure of the red phosphorus also enhances the stability of solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) layer, which is confirmed by the microscopy and impedance spectroscopy after the cycling tests.  Our studies provide a feasible approach for potentially viable high-capacity NIB anode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201703472"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous Red Phosphorus Embedded in Sandwiched Porous Carbon Enabling Superior Sodium Storage Performances</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1703472</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Template approach to nitrogen-doped hierarchical porous carbon nanospheres from polydopamine for high-performance supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Shuqiang; Fan, Jinchen; Wang, Yan; Zhu, Jing; Yu, Junrong; Hu, Zuming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped hierarchical porous carbon nanospheres (NHPCNs) with mesoscale and microscale pores are reported herein for their application in high-performance supercapacitor electrode materials (SCMs).                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design of Red Phosphorus Nanostructured Electrode for Fast-Charging Lithium-Ion Batteries with High Energy Density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yongming; Wang, Li; Li, Yanbin; Li, Yuzhang; Lee, Hye Ryoung; Pei, Allen; He, Xiangming; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We propose that red phosphorus (P) is an ideal anode material for fast-charging lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because of the combined advantages of high capacity (6,075 mAh cm-3) and relatively low yet safe lithiation potential (∼0.7 V vs. Li/Li+).     <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">736-746</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JOULBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2542-4351</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the rapid development of flexible electronics, low-cost, flexible, high-energy-d. power sources are urgently needed.  Theor., the emerging rechargeable potassium-ion batteries (KIBs) could be a promising candidate due to the abundance and low cost of potassium resources.  However, owing to the absence of high-performance cathode materials and effective methods to fabricate robust and soft electrodes, producing flexible KIBs remains a daunting challenge.  Herein, cyanotype is successfully employed as a photog. printing technique for the fabrication of a low-cost, scalable, and flexible cathode.  The combined advantages of optimized crystallinity and morphol. of the cathode materials as well as the ultralight and robust nature of the flexible electrode endow the KIB with superior performance including high energy d. (up to 232 Wh kg-1) and excellent flexibility.  This low-cost and scalable photog. printing technique as well as the promising electrochem. results will promote the development of flexible electronics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2016.04.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pasta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H. R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbothermic Reduction Synthesis of Red Phosphorus-Filled 3D Carbon Material as a High-Capacity Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Materials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">130</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">136</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.ensm.2016.04.003</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D130-136%26journal%3DEnergy%2BStorage%2BMaterials%26author%3DJ.%2BSun%26author%3DH.%2BLee%26author%3DM.%2BPasta%26author%3DY.%2BSun%26author%3DW.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BR.%2BLee%26author%3DN.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BCui%26title%3DCarbothermic%2BReduction%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BRed%2BPhosphorus-Filled%2B3D%2BCarbon%2BMaterial%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh-Capacity%2BAnode%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.ensm.2016.04.003&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b07428&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.ensm.2016.04.003&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201802386"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Si, Pe.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ci, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Fabrication of Nitrogen-Doped Porous Carbon as Superior Anode Material for Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1802386</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201802386</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D8%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D1802386%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DD.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BRen%26author%3DQ.%2BAi%26author%3DQ.%2BSun%26author%3DL.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DL.%2BZhen%26author%3DR.%2BPeng%26author%3DPe.%2BSi%26author%3DJ.%2BLou%26author%3DJ.%2BFeng%26author%3DL.%2BCi%26title%3DFacile%2BFabrication%2Bof%2BNitrogen-Doped%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2Bas%2BSuperior%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BPotassium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201802386&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b07428&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201802386&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201802753"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ju, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Phosphorus Particles Embedded in Reduced Graphene Oxide Matrix to Enhance Capacity and Rate Capability for Capacitive Potassium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Chem. - Eur. J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>24</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13897</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13902</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/chem.201802753</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D24%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D13897-13902%26journal%3DChem.%2B-%2BEur.%2BJ.%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BXing%26author%3DX.%2BWu%26author%3DW.%2BZhao%26author%3DX.%2BQi%26author%3DZ.%2BJu%26author%3DQ.%2BZhuang%26title%3DPhosphorus%2BParticles%2BEmbedded%2Bin%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2BMatrix%2Bto%2BEnhance%2BCapacity%2Band%2BRate%2BCapability%2Bfor%2BCapacitive%2BPotassium-Ion%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fchem.201802753&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b07428&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fchem.201802753&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus particles embedded in reduced graphene oxide matrix to enhance capacity and rate capability for capacitive potassium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hong; Wang, Lifeng; Wang, Liancheng; Xing, Zheng; Wu, Xuan; Zhao, Wei; Qi, Xiujun; Ju, Zhicheng; Zhuang, Quanchao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">52</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13897-13902</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0947-6539</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Early studies indicate that graphite is feasible as the neg. electrode of a potassium-ion battery, but its electrochem. performance still cannot meet the demands of applications.  More efforts should be focused on increasing the specific capacity and improving the rate capability in the meantime.  Thus, stainless-steel autoclave technol. has been utilized to prep. phosphorus nanoparticles encapsulated in reduced graphene oxide matrix as the electrode materials for a potassium-ion battery.  As a result, the composite matrix affords high reversible capacities of 354 and 253 mA h g-1 at 100 and 500 mA g-1, resp.  The superior electrochem. performance is mainly because the composite matrix possesses better electronic cond. and a robust structure, which can promote the electron-transfer performance of the electrode.  Furthermore, phosphorus particles can contribute to the high capacity through an alloying mechanism.  In addn., the silklike, ultrathin, film composite with a high surface area is conducive to capacitive potassium-ion storage, which plays a more important role in rate performance and a high c.d. capability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref39" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.04.037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Si, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ci, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchically Porous Carbon Supported Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> as a Superior Anode Material for Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Materials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>23</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">367</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">374</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.ensm.2019.04.037</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D23%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D367-374%26journal%3DEnergy%2BStorage%2BMaterials%26author%3DD.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DQ.%2BSun%26author%3DS.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BLiang%26author%3DP.%2BSi%26author%3DL.%2BCi%26title%3DHierarchically%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2BSupported%2BSn4P3%2Bas%2Ba%2BSuperior%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BPotassium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.ensm.2019.04.037&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b07428&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.ensm.2019.04.037&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mesoporous hollow SnO2 nanococoons (mh-SnO2 NCs) were synthesized via the redox reaction between SnCl2 and Fe2O3 nanospindles in the presence of excess SnCl4.  The Fe2O3 nanospindles act as a sacrificial template to oxidize SnCl2 to form a layer of SnO2 on the original Fe2O3 core surface and the following hydrolysis of SnCl4 on the as-generated SnO2 further produces SnO2 nanoparticles (NPs) to solidify the mh-SnO2 shell, resulting in the formation of a hierarchical structure on the surface.  The surface morphol. of mh-SnO2 NCs could be easily controlled by varying the synthesis parameters.  The resulting mh-SnO2 NCs possess superior lithium storage properties with an exceptionally good cycling performance and an excellent rate capability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA07272D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">One-Pot Controllable Synthesis of CoFe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> Solid, Hollow and Multi-Shell Hollow Nanospheres as Superior Anode Materials for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A straightforward and general strategy for the large-scale synthesis of hollow metal oxide shells with controlled size, compn. and internal structure is highly desirable owing to their significant applications in energy storage devices such as lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  In this work, we design for the first time a one-pot and cost-effective method to controllably fabricate CoFe2O4 solid nanospheres (CFO-SNSs), CoFe2O4 hollow nanospheres (CFO-HNSs) and multi-shell CoFe2O4 hollow nanospheres (MS-CFO-HNSs) on a large scale by just varying the calcination conditions.  Compared with CFO-SNSs and CFO-HNSs, as anode materials for LIBs, MS-CFO-HNSs deliver a superior lithium storage capacity, which stabilize at a reversible capacity as high as 1354 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at a c.d. of 500 mA g-1.  Even at the high current densities of 1000 and 5000 mA g-1, the specific capacities of MS-CFO-HNSs are still up to 1041 and 570 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles (88.9% and 86.9% of the capacity retention), which break the previous records and exhibit the best cycling performance among the as-reported ternary transition metal oxide (TTMO) materials with the same structures or ingredients owing to the unique nanoscale size of MS-CFO-HNSs, thus providing a preview of their practical applications in LIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201200791"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Selected-Control Synthesis of Monodisperse Fe<sub>3</sub>O<sub>4</sub>@C Core-Shell Spheres, Chains, and Rings as High-Performance Anode Materials for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. - Eur.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The colloidal routes are reported to synthesize silicon@carbon composites for the first time.  Surface-functionalized Si nanoparticles (SiNPs) dissolved in styrene and hexadecane are used as the dispersed phase in oil-in-water emulsions, from which yolk-shell and dual-shell hollow SiNPs@C composites are produced via polymn. and subsequent carbonization.  As anode materials for Li-ion batteries, the SiNPs@C composites demonstrate excellent cycling stability and rate performance, which is ascribed to the uniform distribution of SiNPs within the carbon hosts.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Polydopamine (PDA), which is biodegradable and is derived from naturally occurring products, can be employed as an electrode material, wherein controllable partial oxidization plays a key role in balancing the proportion of redox-active carbonyl groups and the structural stability and cond.                 10.1002/adma.201700214</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA07683E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuen, M. F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced Cycling Stability of Ring-Shaped Phosphorus inside Multi-Walled Carbon Nanotubes as Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2540</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2548</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7TA07683E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced cycling stability of ring-shaped phosphorus inside multi-walled carbon nanotubes as anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Dan; Zhang, Jinying; Fu, Chengcheng; Huang, Jialiang; Xiao, Dingbin; Yuen, Matthew M. F.; Niu, Chunming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2540-2548</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A ring-shaped phosphorus allotrope has recently been synthesized inside multi-walled carbon nanotubes (r-P@MWCNTs).  The electrochem. properties of the r-P@MWCNTs as anodes for lithium-ion batteries were investigated.  External phosphorus was found to degrade rapidly during charging and discharging cycles.  The internal ring-shaped phosphorus is well stabilized by the surrounding carbon nanotube walls to provide an extremely high cycling stability.  The specific capacities of r-P@MWCNTs degrade in the first dozens of cycles and then tend to be stable.  The insertion and extn. of lithium ions through MWCNTs to the encapsulated phosphorus are believed to occur through the defects and interlayer gaps of MWCNTs.  The vol. expansion of phosphorus during lithiation is eased along the axis of MWCNTs since the MWCNTs are not fully filled by phosphorus; this prevents the encapsulated phosphorus from escaping and further resulting in capacity degrdn.  A specific capacity of 444 mA h g-1 based on the whole composites, contg. ∼16% phosphorus, is still maintained after 500 cycles at a current rate of 500 mA g-1.  The electrochem. performances of ring-shaped phosphorus inside MWCNTs were demonstrated to be much higher than those of different phosphorus phases grown on the outside surfaces of MWCNTs under same conditions.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.8b04957"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Boosting Potassium-Ion Battery Performance by Encapsulating Red Phosphorus in Free-Standing Nitrogen-Doped Porous Hollow Carbon Nanofibers</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>19</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1351</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1358</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.8b04957</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting Potassium-Ion Battery Performance by Encapsulating Red Phosphorus in Free-Standing Nitrogen-Doped Porous Hollow Carbon Nanofibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Ying; Hu, Shuhe; Xu, Rui; Wang, Jiawei; Peng, Zhangquan; Zhang, Qiaobao; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">19</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1351-1358</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (KIBs) are a promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale renewable energy storage owning to the natural abundance and low cost of potassium.  However, the biggest challenge for KIBs application lies in the lack of suitable electrode materials that can deliver long cycle life and high reversible capacity.  In this work, we realized unprecedented long cycle life with high reversible capacity (465 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1 after 800 cycles) as well as outstanding rate capability (342 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1) for KIBs by embedding red P into free-standing nitrogen-doped porous hollow carbon nanofibers (red P@N-PHCNFs).  This design circumvents the problems of pulverization and aggregation of P particles.  The in situ transmission electron microscopy (TEM) investigation reveals the structural robustness of the composite fibers during potassiation.  The formation of P-C chem. bonds as well as nitrogen doping in the carbon matrix can facilitate the sturdy contact and enhance the adsorption energy of P atoms evidenced by DFT results.  In situ Raman and ex situ XRD demonstrate that the final discharge product of the red P@N-PHCNFs is K4P3.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201204877"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, N.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus has come to our attention as the anode material for lithium-ion batteries with high theor. specific capacity of 2596 mAh g-1 due to its earth-abundant and low-cost.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus has received remarkable attention as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries (NIBs) due to its high theor. capacity.  However, its practical application has been impeded by its intrinsic low electronic cond. and large vol. variations during sodiation/desodiation process.  Here, we design a composite to confine nanosized red phosphorus into the hierarchically porous carbon (HPC) walls by a vaporization-condensation strategy.  The mass loading of P in the HPC/P composite is optimized to deliver a reversible specific capacity of 2,202 mAh/gp based on the mass of red P (836 mAh/gcomposite based on the total composite mass), a high capacity retention over 77% after 100 cycles, and excellent rate performance of 929 mAh/gp at 2 C.  The hierarchical porous carbon serves as the conductive networks, downsize the red phosphorus to nanoscale, and provide free space to accommodate the large vol. expansions.  The suppressed mech. failure of the red phosphorus also enhances the stability of solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) layer, which is confirmed by the microscopy and impedance spectroscopy after the cycling tests.  Our studies provide a feasible approach for potentially viable high-capacity NIB anode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201703472"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous Red Phosphorus Embedded in Sandwiched Porous Carbon Enabling Superior Sodium Storage Performances</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1703472</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.201703472</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA05880B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Facile Template Approach to Nitrogen-Doped Hierarchical Porous Carbon Nanospheres from Polydopamine for High-Performance Supercapacitors</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">18242</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">18252</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C7TA05880B</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Template approach to nitrogen-doped hierarchical porous carbon nanospheres from polydopamine for high-performance supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Shuqiang; Fan, Jinchen; Wang, Yan; Zhu, Jing; Yu, Junrong; Hu, Zuming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18242-18252</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped hierarchical porous carbon nanospheres (NHPCNs) with mesoscale and microscale pores are reported herein for their application in high-performance supercapacitor electrode materials (SCMs).  The NHPCNs were facilely prepd. via the carbonization of mesoporous polydopamine nanospheres (MPNSs) fabricated by one-step self-polymn. of dopamine using Pluronic F127 as a soft template.  The influence of polymn. and carbonation temps. on the morphologies, structures, and capacitor performances of the as-prepd. NHPCNs was investigated systematically.  The sp. surface area of the NHPCNs can be achieved as high as 1725 m2 g-1, together with a pore vol. of 1.85 cm3 g-1.  Due to their unique structure, the NHPCNs can act as high-performance SCMs and exhibit high charge storage capacity with a high specific capacitance of 433 F g-1 in 6 M KOH at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1 and excellent stability with 95.7% of the initial capacitance after 10 000 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.joule.2019.01.017"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.                 10.1016/j.joule.2019.01.017</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design of Red Phosphorus Nanostructured Electrode for Fast-Charging Lithium-Ion Batteries with High Energy Density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Yongming; Wang, Li; Li, Yanbin; Li, Yuzhang; Lee, Hye Ryoung; Pei, Allen; He, Xiangming; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1080-1093</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JOULBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2542-4351</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We propose that red phosphorus (P) is an ideal anode material for fast-charging lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) because of the combined advantages of high capacity (6,075 mAh cm-3) and relatively low yet safe lithiation potential (∼0.7 V vs. Li/Li+).  A red P/C nanocomposite has been fabricated, featuring amorphous red P nanodomains embedded in the nanopores of micrometer-scale porous conductive carbon with interior nanoscale void spaces, a conductive P-free carbon superficial layer, and a high tap d. of 1.0 g cm-3.  At an industrial-level areal capacity (3 mAh cm-2 or higher), a P/C electrode shows considerably better fast-charging capability than com. graphite and Li4Ti5O12 electrodes, as well as much higher volumetric capacity and specific capacity based on the whole electrode.  Meanwhile, our P/C electrode shows excellent long-term cycling stability with Coulombic efficiency of 100.0% (±0.1%) and 90% capacity retention from the 5th to 500th cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.joule.2018.01.010"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Energy-Density Flexible Potassium-Ion Battery Based on Patterned Electrodes</span>. <i>Joule</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">736</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">746</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.joule.2018.01.010</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Energy-Density Flexible Potassium-Ion Battery Based on Patterned Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yun-Hai; Yang, Xu; Bao, Di; Bie, Xiao-Fei; Sun, Tao; Wang, Sai; Jiang, Yin-Shan; Zhang, Xin-Bo; Yan, Jun-Min; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">736-746</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JOULBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2542-4351</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">With the rapid development of flexible electronics, low-cost, flexible, high-energy-d. power sources are urgently needed.  Theor., the emerging rechargeable potassium-ion batteries (KIBs) could be a promising candidate due to the abundance and low cost of potassium resources.  However, owing to the absence of high-performance cathode materials and effective methods to fabricate robust and soft electrodes, producing flexible KIBs remains a daunting challenge.  Herein, cyanotype is successfully employed as a photog. printing technique for the fabrication of a low-cost, scalable, and flexible cathode.  The combined advantages of optimized crystallinity and morphol. of the cathode materials as well as the ultralight and robust nature of the flexible electrode endow the KIB with superior performance including high energy d. (up to 232 Wh kg-1) and excellent flexibility.  This low-cost and scalable photog. printing technique as well as the promising electrochem. results will promote the development of flexible electronics.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2016.04.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pasta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, H.                 10.1016/j.ensm.2016.04.003</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

J.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>24</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13897</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13902</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/chem.201802753</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus particles embedded in reduced graphene oxide matrix to enhance capacity and rate capability for capacitive potassium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Hong; Wang, Lifeng; Wang, Liancheng; Xing, Zheng; Wu, Xuan; Zhao, Wei; Qi, Xiujun; Ju, Zhicheng; Zhuang, Quanchao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">24</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">52</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13897-13902</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CEUJED</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Early studies indicate that graphite is feasible as the neg. electrode of a potassium-ion battery, but its electrochem. performance still cannot meet the demands of applications.  More efforts should be focused on increasing the specific capacity and improving the rate capability in the meantime.  Thus, stainless-steel autoclave technol. has been utilized to prep. phosphorus nanoparticles encapsulated in reduced graphene oxide matrix as the electrode materials for a potassium-ion battery.  As a result, the composite matrix affords high reversible capacities of 354 and 253 mA h g-1 at 100 and 500 mA g-1, resp.  The superior electrochem. performance is mainly because the composite matrix possesses better electronic cond. and a robust structure, which can promote the electron-transfer performance of the electrode.  Furthermore, phosphorus particles can contribute to the high capacity through an alloying mechanism.  In addn., the silklike, ultrathin, film composite with a high surface area is conducive to capacitive potassium-ion storage, which plays a more important role in rate performance and a high c.d. capability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.04.037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Si, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ci, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchically Porous Carbon Supported Sn<sub>4</sub>P<sub>3</sub> as a Superior Anode Material for Potassium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Materials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>23</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">367</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">374</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        <script nonce="9318a749bdd6222a-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="9318a749bdd6222a-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();

<script nonce="9318a749bdd6222a-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      var emailValid = "",

        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();

          //   console.log(event.target);

        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");

          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>

        <script nonce="9318a749bdd6222a-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Nano";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");

                    cookie=status;

    })
